Development Guide\n\n\u003cdetails\u003e\n\u003csummary\u003eRelevant source files\u003c/summary\u003e\n\nThe following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:\n\n- [.github/workflows/rust.yml](.github/workflows/rust.yml)\n- [CONTRIBUTING.md](CONTRIBUTING.md)\n- [Cargo.toml](Cargo.toml)\n- [README.md](README.md)\n- [justfile](justfile)\n\n\u003c/details\u003e\n\n\n\nThis document provides a comprehensive guide for developers contributing to the 3DCrate project. It covers the development workflow, tooling, project conventions, testing practices, and CI/CD pipeline. The guide focuses on practical development tasks and the specific tools and commands used in the 3DCrate ecosystem.\n\nFor information about the overall system architecture and design principles, see [Architecture \u0026 Design](#3). For detailed API documentation of individual crates, see [Crates Reference](#4).\n\n## Development Environment Setup\n\nThe 3DCrate project uses a modern Rust development stack with automated tooling for quality assurance and development workflow management.\n\n### Prerequisites\n\nThe project requires Rust 1.70+ and uses the 2024 Rust edition as specified in the workspace configuration. GPU-accelerated features will require DirectX 11+, Vulkan 1.1+, or Metal 2.0+ support.\n\n### Development Tools Installation\n\nThe project provides automated tool installation through the `justfile` command runner:\n\n```bash\njust install-tools\n```\n\nThis installs essential development tools including `cargo-machete` for unused dependency detection and `just` for command automation.\n\n**Development Tools Stack**\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph \"Development Environment\"\n        rust[\"Rust 1.70+\u003cbr/\u003eEdition 2024\"]\n        just[\"just\u003cbr/\u003eCommand Runner\"]\n        machete[\"cargo-machete\u003cbr/\u003eDependency Analysis\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Quality Tools\"\n        rustfmt[\"rustfmt\u003cbr/\u003eCode Formatting\"]\n        clippy[\"clippy\u003cbr/\u003eLinting \u0026 Analysis\"]\n        test[\"cargo test\u003cbr/\u003eTest Runner\"]\n        doc[\"cargo doc\u003cbr/\u003eDocumentation\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"CI/CD Tools\"\n        github[\"GitHub Actions\u003cbr/\u003eCI Pipeline\"]\n        perf[\"perf\u003cbr/\u003ePerformance Profiling\"]\n        criterion[\"criterion\u003cbr/\u003eBenchmarking\"]\n    end\n    \n    rust --\u003e just\n    rust --\u003e rustfmt\n    rust --\u003e clippy\n    rust --\u003e test\n    rust --\u003e doc\n    just --\u003e machete\n    github --\u003e rust\n```\n\nSources: [justfile:84-85](), [Cargo.toml:15-17](), [.github/workflows/rust.yml:1-23]()\n\n## Development Workflow\n\nThe development workflow is managed through the `justfile` which provides standardized commands for common development tasks. The primary workflow patterns are rapid iteration (`just dev`) and pre-commit validation (`just ready`).\n\n### Daily Development Commands\n\n**Quick Development Cycle**\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    subgraph \"just dev\"\n        fmt[\"cargo fmt --all\u003cbr/\u003eCode Formatting\"]\n        check[\"cargo check --workspace\u003cbr/\u003eFast Compilation Check\"]\n        test[\"cargo test --workspace\u003cbr/\u003eRun Tests\"]\n    end\n    \n    fmt --\u003e check\n    check --\u003e test\n    \n    subgraph \"Files Modified\"\n        source[\"Source Files\u003cbr/\u003e*.rs\"]\n        config[\"Config Files\u003cbr/\u003eCargo.toml\"]\n    end\n    \n    source --\u003e fmt\n    config --\u003e fmt\n```\n\n**Pre-Commit Validation**\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    subgraph \"just ready\"\n        fmt2[\"cargo fmt --all\u003cbr/\u003eFormat Code\"]\n        clippy[\"cargo clippy\u003cbr/\u003eLint \u0026 Best Practices\"]\n        test2[\"cargo test --workspace\u003cbr/\u003eFull Test Suite\"]\n    end\n    \n    fmt2 --\u003e clippy\n    clippy --\u003e test2\n    \n    ready_result[\"Ready for Commit\"]\n    test2 --\u003e ready_result\n```\n\n### Command Reference\n\n| Command | Purpose | Usage |\n|---------|---------|-------|\n| `just dev` | Quick development cycle | Format, check, test |\n| `just ready` | Pre-commit validation | Format, clippy, test |\n| `just pr-ready` | Full quality check | Clean, format, clippy, test, doc |\n| `just ci` | CI checks locally | Format check, clippy, test |\n| `just example` | Run basic usage example | Execute `basic_usage` binary |\n\nSources: [justfile:107](), [justfile:53](), [justfile:110](), [justfile:50](), [justfile:60]()\n\n## Project Structure and Conventions\n\nThe 3DCrate project follows a multi-crate workspace architecture with clear separation of concerns and consistent naming conventions.\n\n### Workspace Architecture\n\n**Crate Organization**\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph \"Workspace Root\"\n        cargo_toml[\"Cargo.toml\u003cbr/\u003eWorkspace Configuration\"]\n        justfile_node[\"justfile\u003cbr/\u003eDevelopment Commands\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Core Crates\"\n        core[\"threecrate-core\u003cbr/\u003eData Structures\"]\n        algorithms[\"threecrate-algorithms\u003cbr/\u003eProcessing Algorithms\"]\n        io[\"threecrate-io\u003cbr/\u003eFile I/O Operations\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Specialized Crates\"\n        gpu[\"threecrate-gpu\u003cbr/\u003eGPU Acceleration\"]\n        reconstruction[\"threecrate-reconstruction\u003cbr/\u003eSurface Reconstruction\"]\n        simplification[\"threecrate-simplification\u003cbr/\u003eMesh Simplification\"]\n        visualization[\"threecrate-visualization\u003cbr/\u003e3D Rendering\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Development\"\n        examples[\"examples/\u003cbr/\u003eUsage Examples\"]\n        ci[\"github/workflows/\u003cbr/\u003eCI Configuration\"]\n    end\n    \n    cargo_toml --\u003e core\n    cargo_toml --\u003e algorithms\n    cargo_toml --\u003e io\n    cargo_toml --\u003e gpu\n    cargo_toml --\u003e reconstruction\n    cargo_toml --\u003e simplification\n    cargo_toml --\u003e visualization\n    cargo_toml --\u003e examples\n```\n\n### Naming Conventions\n\nAll crates follow the `threecrate-*` naming pattern with consistent internal structure:\n\n- **Public API**: Exposed through `lib.rs` with clear module organization\n- **Error Types**: Standardized `ProcessingError` and domain-specific error types\n- **Test Modules**: Co-located with implementation using `#[cfg(test)]`\n- **Documentation**: Comprehensive API docs with complexity notes and examples\n\n### Dependency Management\n\nThe workspace uses centralized dependency management with shared versions across all crates:\n\n| Category | Dependencies | Purpose |\n|----------|--------------|---------|\n| Core | `nalgebra`, `glam`, `bytemuck` | Linear algebra and math operations |\n| Algorithms | `rayon`, `kdtree`, `kiddo`, `ndarray` | Parallel processing and spatial data structures |\n| GPU | `wgpu`, `pollster` | Cross-platform GPU computing |\n| I/O | `obj-rs`, `ply-rs` | 3D file format support |\n| Development | `criterion`, `approx` | Benchmarking and testing |\n\nSources: [Cargo.toml:4-13](), [Cargo.toml:27-56](), [CONTRIBUTING.md:29-40]()\n\n## Quality Gates and Testing\n\nThe project enforces strict quality gates through automated tooling and comprehensive testing requirements. All code must pass formatting, linting, and testing before integration.\n\n### Quality Gate Pipeline\n\n**Automated Quality Checks**\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    subgraph \"Code Quality Gates\"\n        fmt_check[\"rustfmt --check\u003cbr/\u003eFormat Validation\"]\n        clippy_check[\"clippy --all-targets\u003cbr/\u003eLinting Analysis\"]\n        test_suite[\"cargo test --workspace\u003cbr/\u003eTest Execution\"]\n        doc_build[\"cargo doc --workspace\u003cbr/\u003eDocumentation Build\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Quality Metrics\"\n        compilation[\"Compilation Success\u003cbr/\u003eAll Crates Build\"]\n        warnings[\"Zero Clippy Warnings\u003cbr/\u003eBest Practices Enforced\"]\n        test_pass[\"All Tests Pass\u003cbr/\u003eFunctionality Verified\"]\n        doc_complete[\"Documentation Complete\u003cbr/\u003eAPI Coverage\"]\n    end\n    \n    fmt_check --\u003e compilation\n    clippy_check --\u003e warnings\n    test_suite --\u003e test_pass\n    doc_build --\u003e doc_complete\n    \n    subgraph \"Gate Results\"\n        pass[\"Quality Gate PASS\u003cbr/\u003eReady for Integration\"]\n        fail[\"Quality Gate FAIL\u003cbr/\u003eRequires Fixes\"]\n    end\n    \n    compilation --\u003e pass\n    warnings --\u003e pass\n    test_pass --\u003e pass\n    doc_complete --\u003e pass\n    \n    compilation --\u003e fail\n    warnings --\u003e fail\n    test_pass --\u003e fail\n    doc_complete --\u003e fail\n```\n\n### Testing Requirements\n\nAll new algorithms and functionality must include comprehensive tests following the established patterns:\n\n```rust\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use threecrate_core::{PointCloud, Point3f};\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_algorithm_name() {\n        let points = vec![\n            Point3f::new(0.0, 0.0, 0.0),\n            Point3f::new(1.0, 0.0, 0.0),\n        ];\n        let cloud = PointCloud::from_points(points);\n        \n        let result = your_algorithm(\u0026cloud);\n        assert!(result.is_ok());\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Performance Monitoring\n\nThe project includes infrastructure for performance monitoring and benchmarking:\n\n- **Criterion Benchmarks**: HTML report generation for performance tracking\n- **Performance Profiling**: Linux `perf` integration for detailed analysis\n- **Memory Efficiency**: Focus on cache-friendly data structures\n\nSources: [justfile:49-53](), [CONTRIBUTING.md:89-107](), [justfile:87-95](), [Cargo.toml:56]()\n\n## CI/CD Pipeline\n\nThe continuous integration pipeline ensures code quality and build verification across all supported platforms using GitHub Actions.\n\n### CI Pipeline Configuration\n\n**GitHub Actions Workflow**\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    subgraph \"Trigger Events\"\n        push_main[\"Push to main\u003cbr/\u003eBranch Protection\"]\n        pull_request[\"Pull Request\u003cbr/\u003eCode Review\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"CI Jobs\"\n        ubuntu[\"ubuntu-latest\u003cbr/\u003eBuild Environment\"]\n        checkout[\"actions/checkout@v4\u003cbr/\u003eSource Code Fetch\"]\n        build[\"cargo build --verbose\u003cbr/\u003eCompilation Verification\"]\n        test[\"cargo test --verbose\u003cbr/\u003eTest Execution\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Environment\"\n        cargo_color[\"CARGO_TERM_COLOR=always\u003cbr/\u003eTerminal Output\"]\n        rust_toolchain[\"Latest Stable Rust\u003cbr/\u003eDefault Toolchain\"]\n    end\n    \n    push_main --\u003e ubuntu\n    pull_request --\u003e ubuntu\n    ubuntu --\u003e checkout\n    checkout --\u003e build\n    build --\u003e test\n    \n    cargo_color --\u003e build\n    cargo_color --\u003e test\n    rust_toolchain --\u003e build\n```\n\n### Local CI Validation\n\nDevelopers can run the complete CI pipeline locally using the `just ci` command, which executes the same checks as the GitHub Actions workflow:\n\n```bash\njust ci  # Equivalent to: fmt-check clippy test\n```\n\nThis ensures that code passes all quality gates before pushing to the remote repository.\n\n### Build Verification\n\nThe CI pipeline verifies:\n- **Workspace Compilation**: All crates build successfully\n- **Test Execution**: Complete test suite passes\n- **Cross-platform Compatibility**: Ubuntu Linux environment validation\n- **Dependency Resolution**: All workspace dependencies resolve correctly\n\nSources: [.github/workflows/rust.yml:1-23](), [justfile:50]()\n\n## Contribution Process\n\nThe contribution process follows a structured approach with clear requirements for code quality, testing, and documentation. The project welcomes contributions for algorithm implementation, file I/O support, and GPU acceleration features.\n\n### Pre-Submission Checklist\n\n**Before Submitting Pull Requests**\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    subgraph \"Local Development\"\n        branch[\"Feature Branch\u003cbr/\u003egit checkout -b feature\"]\n        implement[\"Implementation\u003cbr/\u003eReplace todo!() placeholders\"]\n        test_local[\"Add Tests\u003cbr/\u003eUnit \u0026 Integration\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Pre-Submission Validation\"\n        rebase[\"git rebase upstream/main\u003cbr/\u003eSync with Latest\"]\n        quality[\"just pr-ready\u003cbr/\u003eFull Quality Check\"]\n        review_self[\"Self Review\u003cbr/\u003eCode \u0026 Documentation\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Submission\"\n        pr_create[\"Create Pull Request\u003cbr/\u003eDescriptive Title\"]\n        pr_description[\"PR Description\u003cbr/\u003eImplementation Details\"]\n        ci_pass[\"CI Pipeline\u003cbr/\u003eAutomated Validation\"]\n    end\n    \n    branch --\u003e implement\n    implement --\u003e test_local\n    test_local --\u003e rebase\n    rebase --\u003e quality\n    quality --\u003e review_self\n    review_self --\u003e pr_create\n    pr_create --\u003e pr_description\n    pr_description --\u003e ci_pass\n```\n\n### Implementation Priorities\n\nThe project maintains a clear priority system for contributions:\n\n**High Priority Tasks**\n- Statistical outlier removal in `threecrate-algorithms/src/filtering.rs`\n- Surface normal estimation in `threecrate-algorithms/src/normals.rs`\n- PLY file reader/writer in `threecrate-io/src/ply.rs`\n- Basic point cloud rendering infrastructure\n\n**Medium Priority Tasks**\n- ICP registration algorithm in `threecrate-algorithms/src/registration.rs`\n- RANSAC plane segmentation in `threecrate-algorithms/src/segmentation.rs`\n- GPU buffer management in `threecrate-gpu`\n\n### Code Style Requirements\n\nAll contributions must adhere to the established code style:\n\n- **Formatting**: `cargo fmt` (enforced)\n- **Linting**: `cargo clippy` (zero warnings required)\n- **Error Handling**: Use `Result\u003cT, ProcessingError\u003e` for fallible operations\n- **Documentation**: Include complexity notes and algorithm references\n- **Testing**: Comprehensive test coverage for all new functionality\n\nSources: [CONTRIBUTING.md:74-84](), [CONTRIBUTING.md:114-117](), [CONTRIBUTING.md:127-139](), [justfile:110]()"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"1e:T2028,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"# Development Workflow\n\n\u003cdetails\u003e\n\u003csummary\u003eRelevant source files\u003c/summary\u003e\n\nThe following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:\n\n- [CONTRIBUTING.md](CONTRIBUTING.md)\n- [Cargo.toml](Cargo.toml)\n- [README.md](README.md)\n- [justfile](justfile)\n\n\u003c/details\u003e\n\n\n\nThis document describes the development tools, local development practices, and quality gates used in the 3DCrate project. It covers the justfile-based command system, development cycles, and code quality requirements.\n\nFor information about the CI/CD pipeline and automated testing, see [CI/CD Pipeline](#5.2).\n\n## Development Tools\n\nThe 3DCrate project uses a `justfile` as the primary development tool interface, providing standardized commands for common development tasks. The justfile serves as a command runner that wraps cargo operations with consistent workflows.\n\n### Core Development Commands\n\nThe development workflow is built around several key justfile commands that combine multiple cargo operations:\n\n| Command | Purpose | Operations |\n|---------|---------|------------|\n| `just dev` | Quick development cycle | `cargo fmt`, `cargo check`, `cargo test` |\n| `just ready` | Pre-commit preparation | `cargo fmt`, `cargo clippy`, `cargo test` |\n| `just pr-ready` | Full PR validation | `cargo clean`, `cargo fmt`, `cargo clippy`, `cargo test`, `cargo doc` |\n| `just ci` | Local CI simulation | `cargo fmt --check`, `cargo clippy`, `cargo test` |\n\n### Development Tool Installation\n\nThe project requires installation of additional development tools:\n\n```bash\njust install-tools  # Installs cargo-machete and just\n```\n\nSources: [justfile:84-85]()\n\n## Local Development Workflow\n\n### Rapid Development Cycle\n\nThe primary development workflow uses the `just dev` command for rapid iteration:\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    Start[\"Start Development\"]\n    Dev[\"just dev\"]\n    Format[\"cargo fmt\"]\n    Check[\"cargo check\"]\n    Test[\"cargo test --workspace\"]\n    Success[\"Development Ready\"]\n    Fix[\"Fix Issues\"]\n    \n    Start --\u003e Dev\n    Dev --\u003e Format\n    Format --\u003e Check\n    Check --\u003e Test\n    Test --\u003e Success\n    Test --\u003e Fix\n    Fix --\u003e Dev\n    \n    style Dev fill:#f9f9f9\n    style Success fill:#e8f5e8\n```\n\n**Rapid Development Cycle**\n\nSources: [justfile:107](), [justfile:34-35](), [justfile:30-31](), [justfile:18-19]()\n\n### Pre-Commit Workflow\n\nBefore committing changes, developers use the `just ready` command to ensure code quality:\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    Ready[\"just ready\"]\n    Fmt[\"cargo fmt\"]\n    Clippy[\"cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets --all-features\"]\n    Test[\"cargo test --workspace\"]\n    Commit[\"Ready for Commit\"]\n    \n    Ready --\u003e Fmt\n    Fmt --\u003e Clippy\n    Clippy --\u003e Test\n    Test --\u003e Commit\n    \n    style Ready fill:#f9f9f9\n    style Commit fill:#e8f5e8\n```\n\n**Pre-Commit Quality Gates**\n\nSources: [justfile:53](), [justfile:34-35](), [justfile:42-43](), [justfile:18-19]()\n\n## Quality Gates and Code Standards\n\n### Code Formatting Standards\n\nAll code must be formatted using `rustfmt` with the project's default configuration:\n\n- **Automatic formatting**: `just fmt` applies formatting\n- **Format checking**: `just fmt-check` validates formatting without changes\n- **CI requirement**: All PRs must pass `cargo fmt --check`\n\n### Linting Requirements\n\nThe project enforces strict linting through Clippy:\n\n- **Standard linting**: `just clippy` runs with workspace-wide checks\n- **Auto-fix**: `just clippy-fix` applies automatic fixes where possible\n- **Comprehensive coverage**: Includes all targets and features\n\n### Testing Requirements\n\nAll code changes must pass the complete test suite:\n\n- **Workspace testing**: `cargo test --workspace` runs all tests\n- **Verbose output**: `just test-verbose` provides detailed test output\n- **Per-crate testing**: `just test-crate \u003ccrate\u003e` for focused testing\n\nSources: [justfile:42-47](), [justfile:34-39](), [justfile:18-23]()\n\n## Command Reference\n\n### Build Commands\n\n| Command | Description | Cargo Equivalent |\n|---------|-------------|------------------|\n| `just build` | Build all workspace crates | `cargo build --workspace` |\n| `just build-release` | Build in release mode | `cargo build --workspace --release` |\n| `just check` | Fast compilation check | `cargo check --workspace` |\n| `just clean` | Clean build artifacts | `cargo clean` |\n\n### Development Commands\n\n| Command | Description | Use Case |\n|---------|-------------|----------|\n| `just dev` | Quick development cycle | Rapid iteration |\n| `just ready` | Pre-commit preparation | Before committing |\n| `just pr-ready` | Full PR validation | Before submitting PR |\n| `just ci` | Local CI simulation | Validate CI locally |\n\n### Documentation Commands\n\n| Command | Description | Output |\n|---------|-------------|--------|\n| `just doc` | Build documentation | Generates docs without dependencies |\n| `just doc-open` | Build and open docs | Opens documentation in browser |\n\n### Utility Commands\n\n| Command | Description | Purpose |\n|---------|-------------|---------|\n| `just machete` | Check unused dependencies | Dependency cleanup |\n| `just update` | Update dependencies | Dependency management |\n| `just example` | Run basic usage example | Quick functionality test |\n\nSources: [justfile:9-74]()\n\n## Development Workflow Integration\n\n### Command Composition\n\nThe justfile commands are designed to compose well with each other and with standard cargo workflows:\n\n```mermaid\ngraph LR\n    subgraph \"Individual Commands\"\n        Fmt[\"cargo fmt\"]\n        Clippy[\"cargo clippy\"]\n        Test[\"cargo test\"]\n        Check[\"cargo check\"]\n        Doc[\"cargo doc\"]\n        Clean[\"cargo clean\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Composite Workflows\"\n        Dev[\"just dev\"]\n        Ready[\"just ready\"]\n        PRReady[\"just pr-ready\"]\n        CI[\"just ci\"]\n    end\n    \n    Dev --\u003e Fmt\n    Dev --\u003e Check\n    Dev --\u003e Test\n    \n    Ready --\u003e Fmt\n    Ready --\u003e Clippy\n    Ready --\u003e Test\n    \n    PRReady --\u003e Clean\n    PRReady --\u003e Fmt\n    PRReady --\u003e Clippy\n    PRReady --\u003e Test\n    PRReady --\u003e Doc\n    \n    CI --\u003e Fmt\n    CI --\u003e Clippy\n    CI --\u003e Test\n```\n\n**Command Composition and Workflow Integration**\n\n### Algorithm Development Workflow\n\nFor implementing new algorithms, the project provides guidance through the `just new-algorithm` command:\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    NewAlg[\"just new-algorithm \u003cname\u003e \u003ccrate\u003e\"]\n    Checklist[\"Implementation Checklist\"]\n    LibRS[\"Add function signature to lib.rs\"]\n    Impl[\"Implement algorithm with documentation\"]\n    Tests[\"Add comprehensive tests\"]\n    Examples[\"Update examples if needed\"]\n    \n    NewAlg --\u003e Checklist\n    Checklist --\u003e LibRS\n    Checklist --\u003e Impl\n    Checklist --\u003e Tests\n    Checklist --\u003e Examples\n    \n    style NewAlg fill:#f9f9f9\n    style Checklist fill:#fff3cd\n```\n\n**Algorithm Development Process**\n\nSources: [justfile:97-104](), [CONTRIBUTING.md:44-71]()\n\n## Performance and Profiling\n\n### Benchmarking Workflow\n\nThe project includes support for performance benchmarking:\n\n```bash\njust bench  # Run workspace benchmarks\n```\n\n### Profiling Support\n\nFor Linux development, the justfile includes profiling commands:\n\n```bash\njust profile \u003cexample\u003e  # Profile specific example with perf\n```\n\nThis command sequence:\n1. Builds the example in release mode\n2. Records performance data with `perf record`\n3. Opens the performance report with `perf report`\n\nSources: [justfile:88-95]()\n\n## Workspace Management\n\n### Multi-Crate Development\n\nThe development workflow supports the workspace structure defined in the root Cargo.toml:\n\n- **Workspace members**: `threecrate-core`, `threecrate-algorithms`, `threecrate-gpu`, `threecrate-io`, `threecrate-reconstruction`, `threecrate-simplification`, `threecrate-visualization`, `examples`\n- **Unified commands**: All justfile commands operate on the entire workspace\n- **Individual crate testing**: `just test-crate \u003ccrate\u003e` for focused development\n\n### Dependency Management\n\nThe workspace uses centralized dependency management:\n\n- **Shared dependencies**: Core dependencies defined in `[workspace.dependencies]`\n- **Version consistency**: All crates use the same versions of shared dependencies\n- **Dependency auditing**: `just machete` identifies unused dependencies\n\nSources: [Cargo.toml:1-57](), [justfile:76-77]()"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"1f:T1c02,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"# CI/CD Pipeline\n\n\u003cdetails\u003e\n\u003csummary\u003eRelevant source files\u003c/summary\u003e\n\nThe following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:\n\n- [.github/workflows/rust.yml](.github/workflows/rust.yml)\n- [justfile](justfile)\n\n\u003c/details\u003e\n\n\n\nThis document covers the continuous integration and deployment setup for the 3DCrate project, including the GitHub Actions workflow, local quality gates, and development tooling. The CI/CD pipeline ensures code quality, automated testing, and consistent build processes across the workspace.\n\nFor information about local development practices and tooling setup, see [Development Workflow](#5.1).\n\n## GitHub Actions Workflow\n\nThe project uses a single GitHub Actions workflow defined in `.github/workflows/rust.yml` that provides automated CI for all code changes. The workflow is triggered on pushes and pull requests to the main branch.\n\n### CI Pipeline Flow\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    trigger[\"Push/PR to main branch\"]\n    checkout[\"actions/checkout@v4\"]\n    build[\"cargo build --verbose\"]\n    test[\"cargo test --verbose\"]\n    success[\"âœ… CI Success\"]\n    failure[\"âŒ CI Failure\"]\n\n    trigger --\u003e checkout\n    checkout --\u003e build\n    build --\u003e test\n    test --\u003e success\n    test --\u003e failure\n\n    build -.-\u003e failure\n```\n\nThe workflow consists of these essential steps:\n- **Checkout**: Uses `actions/checkout@v4` to retrieve the repository code\n- **Build**: Executes `cargo build --verbose` to compile all workspace crates  \n- **Test**: Runs `cargo test --verbose` to execute the full test suite\n\nThe pipeline runs on `ubuntu-latest` with `CARGO_TERM_COLOR: always` environment variable set for colored output.\n\nSources: [.github/workflows/rust.yml:1-23]()\n\n## Local Quality Gates\n\nThe `justfile` defines multiple quality gate commands that developers can run locally to ensure code meets standards before pushing. These commands mirror and extend the CI pipeline checks.\n\n### Quality Gate Hierarchy\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TB\n    subgraph \"Quick Development\"\n        dev[\"just dev\"]\n        devSteps[\"fmt + check + test\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Pre-commit Ready\"  \n        ready[\"just ready\"]\n        readySteps[\"fmt + clippy + test\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"CI Validation\"\n        ci[\"just ci\"] \n        ciSteps[\"fmt-check + clippy + test\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"PR Ready\"\n        prReady[\"just pr-ready\"]\n        prSteps[\"clean + fmt + clippy + test + doc\"]\n    end\n\n    dev --\u003e devSteps\n    ready --\u003e readySteps  \n    ci --\u003e ciSteps\n    prReady --\u003e prSteps\n```\n\n### Quality Check Commands\n\n| Command | Purpose | Components | Use Case |\n|---------|---------|------------|----------|\n| `just dev` | Quick development cycle | `fmt + check + test` | Rapid iteration during development |\n| `just ready` | Pre-commit validation | `fmt + clippy + test` | Before committing changes |\n| `just ci` | CI simulation | `fmt-check + clippy + test` | Local CI validation |\n| `just pr-ready` | Full quality check | `clean + fmt + clippy + test + doc` | Before creating pull requests |\n\nSources: [justfile:49-50, 52-53, 109-110, 116-118]()\n\n## Development Tools Integration\n\nThe CI/CD pipeline integrates with several Rust ecosystem tools to maintain code quality and consistency.\n\n### Core Quality Tools\n\n```mermaid\ngraph LR\n    subgraph \"Formatting\"\n        rustfmt[\"cargo fmt\"]\n        fmtCheck[\"cargo fmt --check\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Linting\"  \n        clippy[\"cargo clippy\"]\n        clippyFix[\"cargo clippy --fix\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Testing\"\n        test[\"cargo test\"]\n        testVerbose[\"cargo test --nocapture\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Build Verification\"\n        check[\"cargo check\"]\n        build[\"cargo build\"]\n        buildRelease[\"cargo build --release\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Documentation\"\n        doc[\"cargo doc\"]\n        docOpen[\"cargo doc --open\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Dependency Management\"\n        machete[\"cargo machete\"]\n        update[\"cargo update\"]\n    end\n```\n\n### Tool Configuration\n\nThe quality tools are configured with workspace-wide flags:\n\n- **Clippy**: `--workspace --all-targets --all-features` for comprehensive linting\n- **Format**: `--all` to format all workspace members\n- **Test**: `--workspace` to run tests across all crates\n- **Build**: `--workspace` for complete workspace compilation\n\nSources: [justfile:34-47]()\n\n## Workflow Commands\n\nThe justfile provides commands for different development scenarios and workflow stages.\n\n### Build and Test Commands\n\n| Command | Description | Flags |\n|---------|-------------|-------|\n| `build` | Build all workspace crates | `--workspace` |\n| `build-release` | Release mode build | `--workspace --release` |\n| `test` | Run all tests | `--workspace` |\n| `test-verbose` | Tests with output | `--workspace -- --nocapture` |\n| `test-crate \u003cname\u003e` | Test specific crate | `-p \u003ccrate\u003e` |\n| `check` | Fast compilation check | `--workspace` |\n\n### Example and Documentation Commands\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    subgraph \"Examples\"\n        example[\"just example\"]\n        runExample[\"just run-example \u003cname\u003e\"]\n        basicUsage[\"cargo run --bin basic_usage\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Documentation\"\n        doc[\"just doc\"]\n        docOpen[\"just doc-open\"] \n        cargoDoc[\"cargo doc --workspace --no-deps\"]\n    end\n    \n    example --\u003e basicUsage\n    runExample --\u003e basicUsage\n    doc --\u003e cargoDoc\n    docOpen --\u003e cargoDoc\n```\n\nSources: [justfile:59-73]()\n\n## Performance and Profiling\n\nThe CI/CD setup includes commands for performance analysis and profiling, though these are primarily for local development use.\n\n### Profiling Commands\n\n- **Benchmark**: `just bench` runs `cargo bench --workspace` for performance testing\n- **Profile**: `just profile \u003cexample\u003e` creates performance profiles using `perf` on Linux\n- **Release Build**: Optimized builds for performance testing\n\nThe profiling workflow builds release binaries, records execution with `perf record --call-graph=dwarf`, and generates reports with `perf report`.\n\nSources: [justfile:87-95]()\n\n## Development Tool Installation\n\nThe pipeline supports automatic installation of required development tools through the `install-tools` command:\n\n```bash\ncargo install cargo-machete just\n```\n\nThis ensures developers have access to:\n- `cargo-machete` for unused dependency detection\n- `just` command runner for workflow automation\n\nSources: [justfile:83-85]()\n\n## Workspace Integration\n\nThe CI/CD pipeline is designed to work with the multi-crate workspace structure of 3DCrate. All commands operate at the workspace level using the `--workspace` flag, ensuring consistent behavior across all crates.\n\n### Workspace-Level Operations\n\n- **Build**: Compiles all crates including `threecrate-core`, `threecrate-io`, `threecrate-reconstruction`, etc.\n- **Test**: Runs tests for all crates and their integration points\n- **Format/Lint**: Applies consistent code style across the entire workspace\n- **Documentation**: Generates unified documentation for all public APIs\n\nThe workspace configuration ensures that CI/CD operations maintain consistency across the modular architecture while allowing individual crate development.\n\nSources: [justfile:10-19, 29-31, <p>This document introduces the 3DCrate ecosystem, a modular Rust library for 3D point cloud processing and geometric computation. It explains the relationships between the various crates that comprise the system and their roles in the overall architecture.</p>
<p>3DCrate provides a comprehensive toolkit for point cloud manipulation, surface reconstruction, mesh processing, and real-time visualization. The library is designed with modularity and performance as primary goals, separating concerns across specialized crates while maintaining a unified API.</p>
<p>For specific implementation details of individual crates, see <a href="https://deepwiki.com/rajgandhi1/3DCrate/4-crates-reference" class="text-neutral-300 hover:text-neutral-200 hover:underline">Crates Reference</a>. For development setup and contribution guidelines, see <a href="https://deepwiki.com/rajgandhi1/3DCrate/5-development-guide" class="text-neutral-300 hover:text-neutral-200 hover:underline">Development Guide</a>.</p>
<h2 id="system-architecture" class="group flex items-center" data-header="true">System Architecture<button class="relative ml-2 cursor-pointer text-gray-400 opacity-0 transition-opacity hover:text-blue-400 focus:opacity-100 group-hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy link to header"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M117.18,188.74a12,12,0,0,1,0,17l-5.12,5.12A58.26,58.26,0,0,1,70.6,228h0A58.62,58.62,0,0,1,29.14,127.92L63.89,93.17a58.64,58.64,0,0,1,98.56,28.11,12,12,0,1,1-23.37,5.44,34.65,34.65,0,0,0-58.22-16.58L46.11,144.89A34.62,34.62,0,0,0,70.57,204h0a34.41,34.41,0,0,0,24.49-10.14l5.11-5.12A12,12,0,0,1,117.18,188.74ZM226.83,45.17a58.65,58.65,0,0,0-82.93,0l-5.11,5.11a12,12,0,0,0,17,17l5.12-5.12a34.63,34.63,0,1,1,49,49L175.1,145.86A34.39,34.39,0,0,1,150.61,156h0a34.63,34.63,0,0,1-33.69-26.72,12,12,0,0,0-23.38,5.44A58.64,58.64,0,0,0,150.56,180h.05a58.28,58.28,0,0,0,41.47-17.17l34.75-34.75a58.62,58.62,0,0,0,0-82.91Z"></path></svg></button></h2>
<p>The 3DCrate workspace follows a layered architecture with clear separation of concerns across eight specialized crates. The <code class="rounded-sm bg-[#e5e5e5] px-[0.25rem] py-[0.20rem] text-xs font-normal leading-[15px] before:hidden after:hidden dark:bg-[#484848]/30">threecrate-core</code> crate provides foundational data structures, while specialized crates build upon these primitives to offer domain-specific functionality.</p>
<h3 id="workspace-structure" class="group flex items-center" data-header="true">Workspace Structure<button class="relative ml-2 cursor-pointer text-gray-400 opacity-0 transition-opacity hover:text-blue-400 focus:opacity-100 group-hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy link to header"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M117.18,188.74a12,12,0,0,1,0,17l-5.12,5.12A58.26,58.26,0,0,1,70.6,228h0A58.62,58.62,0,0,1,29.14,127.92L63.89,93.17a58.64,58.64,0,0,1,98.56,28.11,12,12,0,1,1-23.37,5.44,34.65,34.65,0,0,0-58.22-16.58L46.11,144.89A34.62,34.62,0,0,0,70.57,204h0a34.41,34.41,0,0,0,24.49-10.14l5.11-5.12A12,12,0,0,1,117.18,188.74ZM226.83,45.17a58.65,58.65,0,0,0-82.93,0l-5.11,5.11a12,12,0,0,0,17,17l5.12-5.12a34.63,34.63,0,1,1,49,49L175.1,145.86A34.39,34.39,0,0,1,150.61,156h0a34.63,34.63,0,0,1-33.69-26.72,12,12,0,0,0-23.38,5.44A58.64,58.64,0,0,0,150.56,180h.05a58.28,58.28,0,0,0,41.47-17.17l34.75-34.75a58.62,58.62,0,0,0,0-82.91Z"></path></svg></button></h3>

<h3 id="data-flow-architecture" class="group flex items-center" data-header="true">Data Flow Architecture<button class="relative ml-2 cursor-pointer text-gray-400 opacity-0 transition-opacity hover:text-blue-400 focus:opacity-100 group-hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy link to header"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M117.18,188.74a12,12,0,0,1,0,17l-5.12,5.12A58.26,58.26,0,0,1,70.6,228h0A58.62,58.62,0,0,1,29.14,127.92L63.89,93.17a58.64,58.64,0,0,1,98.56,28.11,12,12,0,1,1-23.37,5.44,34.65,34.65,0,0,0-58.22-16.58L46.11,144.89A34.62,34.62,0,0,0,70.57,204h0a34.41,34.41,0,0,0,24.49-10.14l5.11-5.12A12,12,0,0,1,117.18,188.74ZM226.83,45.17a58.65,58.65,0,0,0-82.93,0l-5.11,5.11a12,12,0,0,0,17,17l5.12-5.12a34.63,34.63,0,1,1,49,49L175.1,145.86A34.39,34.39,0,0,1,150.61,156h0a34.63,34.63,0,0,1-33.69-26.72,12,12,0,0,0-23.38,5.44A58.64,58.64,0,0,0,150.56,180h.05a58.28,58.28,0,0,0,41.47-17.17l34.75-34.75a58.62,58.62,0,0,0,0-82.91Z"></path></svg></button></h3>
<p>The system processes 3D data through a pipeline that transforms raw input through various processing stages to produce output suitable for analysis or visualization.</p>

<h2 id="core-data-structures" class="group flex items-center" data-header="true">Core Data Structures<button class="relative ml-2 cursor-pointer text-gray-400 opacity-0 transition-opacity hover:text-blue-400 focus:opacity-100 group-hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy link to header"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M117.18,188.74a12,12,0,0,1,0,17l-5.12,5.12A58.26,58.26,0,0,1,70.6,228h0A58.62,58.62,0,0,1,29.14,127.92L63.89,93.17a58.64,58.64,0,0,1,98.56,28.11,12,12,0,1,1-23.37,5.44,34.65,34.65,0,0,0-58.22-16.58L46.11,144.89A34.62,34.62,0,0,0,70.57,204h0a34.41,34.41,0,0,0,24.49-10.14l5.11-5.12A12,12,0,0,1,117.18,188.74ZM226.83,45.17a58.65,58.65,0,0,0-82.93,0l-5.11,5.11a12,12,0,0,0,17,17l5.12-5.12a34.63,34.63,0,1,1,49,49L175.1,145.86A34.39,34.39,0,0,1,150.61,156h0a34.63,34.63,0,0,1-33.69-26.72,12,12,0,0,0-23.38,5.44A58.64,58.64,0,0,0,150.56,180h.05a58.28,58.28,0,0,0,41.47-17.17l34.75-34.75a58.62,58.62,0,0,0,0-82.91Z"></path></svg></button></h2>
<p>The <code class="rounded-sm bg-[#e5e5e5] px-[0.25rem] py-[0.20rem] text-xs font-normal leading-[15px] before:hidden after:hidden dark:bg-[#484848]/30">threecrate-core</code> crate defines the fundamental geometric primitives that all other crates operate upon. These structures implement common traits to enable consistent behavior across the ecosystem.</p>



































<table><thead><tr><th>Data Structure</th><th>Purpose</th><th>Key Methods</th><th>Traits</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code class="rounded-sm bg-[#e5e5e5] px-[0.25rem] py-[0.20rem] text-xs font-normal leading-[15px] before:hidden after:hidden dark:bg-[#484848]/30">PointCloud&lt;T&gt;</code></td><td>Generic point container</td><td><code class="rounded-sm bg-[#e5e5e5] px-[0.25rem] <h2 id="technology-stack" class="group flex items-center" data-header="true">Technology Stack<button class="relative ml-2 cursor-pointer text-gray-400 opacity-0 transition-opacity hover:text-blue-400 focus:opacity-100 group-hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy link to header"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M117.18,188.74a12,12,0,0,1,0,17l-5.12,5.12A58.26,58.26,0,0,1,70.6,228h0A58.62,58.62,0,0,1,29.14,127.92L63.89,93.17a58.64,58.64,0,0,1,98.56,28.11,12,12,0,1,1-23.37,5.44,34.65,34.65,0,0,0-58.22-16.58L46.11,144.89A34.62,34.62,0,0,0,70.57,204h0a34.41,34.41,0,0,0,24.49-10.14l5.11-5.12A12,12,0,0,1,117.18,188.74ZM226.83,45.17a58.65,58.65,0,0,0-82.93,0l-5.11,5.11a12,12,0,0,0,17,17l5.12-5.12a34.63,34.63,0,1,1,49,49L175.1,145.86A34.39,34.39,0,0,1,150.61,156h0a34.63,34.63,0,0,1-33.69-26.72,12,12,0,0,0-23.38,5.44A58.64,58.64,0,0,0,150.56,180h.05a58.28,58.28,0,0,0,41.47-17.17l34.75-34.75a58.62,58.62,0,0,0,0-82.91Z"></path></svg></button></h2>
<p>3DCrate leverages a carefully selected set of Rust crates to provide mathematical foundations, GPU acceleration, and cross-platform compatibility.</p>
<h3 id="external-dependencies" class="group flex items-center" data-header="true">External Dependencies<button class="relative ml-2 cursor-pointer text-gray-400 opacity-0 transition-opacity hover:text-blue-400 focus:opacity-100 group-hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy link to header"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M117.18,188.74a12,12,0,0,1,0,17l-5.12,5.12A58.26,58.26,0,0,1,70.6,228h0A58.62,58.62,0,0,1,29.14,127.92L63.89,93.17a58.64,58.64,0,0,1,98.56,28.11,12,12,0,1,1-23.37,5.44,34.65,34.65,0,0,0-58.22-16.58L46.11,144.89A34.62,34.62,0,0,0,70.57,204h0a34.41,34.41,0,0,0,24.49-10.14l5.11-5.12A12,12,0,0,1,117.18,188.74ZM226.83,45.17a58.65,58.65,0,0,0-82.93,0l-5.11,5.11a12,12,0,0,0,17,17l5.12-5.12a34.63,34.63,0,1,1,49,49L175.1,145.86A34.39,34.39,0,0,1,150.61,156h0a34.63,34.63,0,0,1-33.69-26.72,12,12,0,0,0-23.38,5.44A58.64,58.64,0,0,0,150.56,180h.05a58.28,58.28,0,0,0,41.47-17.17l34.75-34.75a58.62,58.62,0,0,0,0-82.91Z"></path></svg></button></h3>

<h2 id="implementation-status" class="group flex items-center" data-header="true">Implementation Status<button class="relative ml-2 cursor-pointer text-gray-400 opacity-0 transition-opacity hover:text-blue-400 focus:opacity-100 group-hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy link to header"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M117.18,188.74a12,12,0,0,1,0,17l-5.12,5.12A58.26,58.26,0,0,1,70.6,228h0A58.62,58.62,0,0,1,29.14,127.92L63.89,93.17a58.64,58.64,0,0,1,98.56,28.11,12,12,0,1,1-23.37,5.44,34.65,34.65,0,0,0-58.22-16.58L46.11,144.89A34.62,34.62,0,0,0,70.57,204h0a34.41,34.41,0,0,0,24.49-10.14l5.11-5.12A12,12,0,0,1,117.18,188.74ZM226.83,45.17a58.65,58.65,0,0,0-82.93,0l-5.11,5.11a12,12,0,0,0,17,17l5.12-5.12a34.63,34.63,0,1,1,49,49L175.1,145.86A34.39,34.39,0,0,1,150.61,156h0a34.63,34.63,0,0,1-33.69-26.72,12,12,0,0,0-23.38,5.44A58.64,58.64,0,0,0,150.56,180h.05a58.28,58.28,0,0,0,41.47-17.17l34.75-34.75a58.62,58.62,0,0,0,0-82.91Z"></path></svg></button></h2>
<p>3DCrate is currently in early development with a functional core infrastructure and skeletal implementations of advanced algorithms. The project prioritizes a solid foundation before implementing complex processing algorithms.</p>
<h3 id="current-implementation-state" class="group flex items-center" data-header="true">Current Implementation State<button class="relative ml-2 cursor-pointer text-gray-400 opacity-0 transition-opacity hover:text-blue-400 focus:opacity-100 group-hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy link to header"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M117.18,188.74a12,12,0,0,1,0,17l-5.12,5.12A58.26,58.26,0,0,1,70.6,228h0A58.62,58.62,0,0,1,29.14,127.92L63.89,93.17a58.64,58.64,0,0,1,98.56,28.11,12,12,0,1,1-23.37,5.44,34.65,34.65,0,0,0-58.22-16.58L46.11,144.89A34.62,34.62,0,0,0,70.57,204h0a34.41,34.41,0,0,0,24.49-10.14l5.11-5.12A12,12,0,0,1,117.18,188.74ZM226.83,45.17a58.65,58.65,0,0,0-82.93,0l-5.11,5.11a12,12,0,0,0,17,17l5.12-5.12a34.63,34.63,0,1,1,49,49L175.1,145.86A34.39,34.39,0,0,1,150.61,156h0a34.63,34.63,0,0,1-33.69-26.72,12,12,0,0,0-23.38,5.44A58.64,58.64,0,0,0,150.56,180h.05a58.28,58.28,0,0,0,41.47-17.17l34.75-34.75a58.62,58.62,0,0,0,0-82.91Z"></path></svg></button></h3>

<p>The library currently provides a solid foundation for 3D point cloud processing with room for algorithm implementation and optimization. The modular architecture enables incremental development while maintaining API stability across the ecosystem.</p></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="hidden overflow-hidden transition-[border-radius] xl:sticky xl:right-0 xl:top-20 xl:block xl:h-[calc(100vh-82px)] xl:w-64 xl:flex-shrink-0 2xl:w-72" style="scrollbar-width: none;"><div class="flex max-h-full w-full flex-shrink-0 flex-col py-6 pt-0 text-sm lg:pb-4 lg:pt-8 xl:w-64 2xl:w-72" style="scrollbar-color: var(--color-night) transparent;"><div><div class="relative mx-4 my-4 rounded-md border border-neutral-200 bg-neutral-100 p-3 text-sm text-neutral-600 dark:border-neutral-800 dark:bg-neutral-900 dark:text-neutral-400"><button class="absolute right-2 top-2 rounded-sm p-1 opacity-70 transition-opacity hover:opacity-100 focus:outline-none focus:ring-2 focus:ring-neutral-400 focus:ring-offset-2"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="1em" height="1em" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 256 256" class="h-4 w-4"><path d="M205.66,194.34a8,8,0,0,1-11.32,11.32L128,139.31,61.66,205.66a8,8,0,0,1-11.32-11.32L116.69,128,50.34,61.66A8,8,0,0,1,61.66,50.34L128,116.69l66.34-66.35a8,8,0,0,1,11.32,11.32L139.31,128Z"></path></svg><span class="sr-only">Dismiss</span></button><p class="text-sm font-medium">Refresh this wiki</p><p class="mt-2 text-sm font-light text-neutral-500 dark:text-neutral-400">This wiki was recently refreshed. **Note**: This project is in early development. Most algorithms are currently skeleton implementations with `todo!()` placeholders. See the implementation status below.

## Architecture

### Core Modules

- **`threecrate-core`** - Core data structures and traits for 3D geometry
- **`threecrate-algorithms`** - Point cloud processing algorithms (filtering, normals, registration)
- **`threecrate-gpu`** - GPU-accelerated computing using WGPU
- **`threecrate-io`** - File I/O support for various 3D formats (PLY, OBJ)
- **`threecrate-reconstruction`** - Surface reconstruction algorithms
- **`threecrate-simplification`** - Mesh and point cloud simplification
- **`threecrate-visualization`** - Real-time 3D visualization

## Implementation Status

###  **Implemented**
- **Core Data Structures**: `PointCloud<T>`, `TriangleMesh`, `Point3f`, `Transform3D`
- **Basic Point Cloud Operations**: Creation, iteration, indexing, transformation
- **Traits**: `Drawable`, `Transformable`, `NearestNeighborSearch`
- **Type System**: Generic point cloud containers with specialized types
- **Build System**: Complete workspace with all crates compiling successfully
- **Basic Examples**: Working example demonstrating core functionality

###  **Under Implementation**
- **File I/O**: PLY and OBJ format support (skeleton structure in place)
- **Visualization**: Camera, renderer, and shader infrastructure (basic structure ready)
- **GPU Infrastructure**: Device management and compute pipeline setup

###  **Planned Features**

#### Point Cloud Processing
- **Filtering**: Statistical outlier removal, voxel grid downsampling
- **Normal Estimation**: Surface normal computation with neighborhood search
- **Registration**: ICP (Iterative Closest Point) alignment
- **Segmentation**: Plane detection and clustering algorithms
- **Feature Detection**: Keypoint extraction and descriptors

#### Surface Reconstruction
- **Poisson Reconstruction**: Robust surface reconstruction from oriented points
- **Ball Pivoting**: Fast triangulation for dense point clouds
- **Alpha Shapes**: Boundary detection and shape reconstruction
- **Delaunay Triangulation**: 2D/3D triangulation algorithms

#### GPU Acceleration
- **Parallel Processing**: GPU-accelerated algorithms using WGPU
- **Memory Management**: Efficient GPU buffer management
- **Cross-Platform**: Vulkan, Metal, DirectX 12, and WebGL support

#### Visualization
- **Real-time Rendering**: Interactive 3D point cloud and mesh visualization
- **Multiple Formats**: Support for various rendering primitives
- **Camera Controls**: Orbit, pan, zoom camera interactions

## Quick Start

Add 3DCrate to your `Cargo.toml`:

```toml
[dependencies]
threecrate-core = "0.1.0"
threecrate-algorithms = "0.1.0"
threecrate-io = "0.1.0"
```

### Basic Usage

```rust
use threecrate_core::{PointCloud, Point3f, Transform3D};

fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {
    // Create a point cloud
    let points = vec![
        Point3f::new(0.0, 0.0, 0.0),
        Point3f::new(1.0, 0.0, 0.0),
        Point3f::new(0.0, 1.0, 0.0),
        Point3f::new(0.0, 0.0, 1.0),
    ];
    
    let mut cloud = PointCloud::from_points(points);
    println!("Created point cloud with {} points", cloud.len());
    
    // Apply transformation
    let transform = Transform3D::identity();
    cloud.transform(&transform);
    
    println!("Transformation applied successfully!");
    Ok(())
}
```


## Examples

Currently available examples:

```bash
# Run the basic usage example (works)
cargo run --bin basic_usage
```


## Building

```bash
# Build all crates
cargo build --workspace

# Run tests (currently no tests implemented)
cargo test --workspace

# Check compilation
cargo check --workspace
```

## Development Roadmap

### Phase 1: Core Implementation (Current)
- [x] Core data structures and traits
- [x] Basic point cloud operations
- [x] Workspace setup and compilation
- [ ] File I/O implementations
- [ ] Basic algorithms (filtering, normals)

### Phase 2: Algorithm Implementation
- [ ] Point cloud filtering algorithms
- [ ] Normal estimation
- [ ] Registration (ICP)
- [ ] Segmentation algorithms

### Phase 3: GPU Acceleration
- [ ] WGPU compute pipeline setup
- [ ] GPU-accelerated filtering
- [ ] GPU-accelerated normal estimation
- [ ] GPU-accelerated ICP

### Phase 4: Advanced Features
- [ ] Surface reconstruction
- [ ] Mesh simplification
- [ ] Real-time visualization
- [ ] Advanced file format support

## Performance Goals

3DCrate aims for high performance through:

- **Zero-cost abstractions**: Minimal runtime overhead
- **SIMD optimization**: Vectorized operations where possible
- **Parallel processing**: Multi-threaded algorithms using Rayon
- **GPU acceleration**: WGPU-based compute shaders
- **Memory efficiency**: Cache-friendly data structures

**Note**: Performance benchmarks will be available once core algorithms are implemented.

## Planned Supported Formats

### Input/Output
- **PLY** - Stanford Polygon Format (skeleton implemented)
- **OBJ** - Wavefront OBJ (skeleton implemented)
- **PCD** - Point Cloud Data (planned)
- **LAS/LAZ** - LIDAR formats (planned)

## Requirements

- **Rust**: 1.70+
- **GPU**: DirectX 11+, Vulkan 1.1+, or Metal 2.0+ (for future GPU features)

## Contributing

We welcome contributions! This project is in early development and there are many opportunities to implement core algorithms.

### Development Setup

```bash
git clone https://github.com/yourusername/3DCrate.git
cd 3DCrate
cargo build --workspace
cargo check --workspace
```

### Contributing Guidelines

- Core algorithms need implementation (currently using `todo!()` placeholders)
- Focus on correctness first, then optimization
- Add tests for new functionality
- Update documentation and examples
